Candidate formulas: 50

GT is a **t-independent** function of **P only**:
\[
0.7213\Big[(-1+P/6.6511)(1-P/13.5381)P + (1-P/13.5381)P + P^{1/3}\Big].
\]
So GT contains a **fractional power term** \(P^{1/3}\) with nonzero coefficient, plus polynomial-in-\(P\) terms up to degree 3. Any matching candidate must (i) be independent of \(t\) for all \(t\), and (ii) be able to represent a \(P^{1/3}\) term (not via logs/exp/Max/Abs unless they can reduce exactly to \(P^{1/3}\) for all real \(P\), which they can’t).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can choose constants to (A) remove any \(t\)-dependence and unwanted nonlinearities, and (B) still reproduce the required \(P^{1/3}\) term.

1. Polynomial + \(P\exp(P\cdot)\) + constant. Can kill exp by setting \(c4=0\), but then it’s a pure polynomial+constant, cannot produce \(P^{1/3}\). **No**.
2. Polynomial + tanh(t). Set tanh coefficient \(c5=0\) to remove \(t\). Remaining is polynomial, no \(P^{1/3}\). **No**.
3. Same: can remove tanh, left with polynomial only. **No**.
4. Has Max(0, P+c5) and tanh. Can set tanh coeff 0 and Max term coeff \(c4=0\), left polynomial only. No \(P^{1/3}\). **No**.
5. Pure polynomial+constant. No \(P^{1/3}\). **No**.

15. Polynomial + rational \(P*c4/(P*c5+1)\) + tanh. Remove tanh via \(c6=0\), remove rational via \(c4=0\) → polynomial only. Rational term cannot become \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\). **No**.

21. Polynomial + \(P*(P*c3)^{c4}\) + \(P e^{P\cdot}\) + t/(t^2+...). Remove t term via \(c8=0\), remove exp via \(c5=0\). Then we have \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4} = \text{const}\cdot P^{c4+1}\). This can make \(P^{1/3}\) only if \(c4+1=1/3\Rightarrow c4=-2/3\), but then the term is \(P^{1/3}\) times a constant **and** the rest is only quadratic/linear; however candidate also has a fixed \(P^2*c0\) term (cannot be removed unless \(c0=0\)) and linear terms. We could set \(c0=0\) and tune linear/quadratic to match GT’s polynomial part, and use the \(P^{c4+1}\) term to match \(P^{1/3}\). Problem: that term is \(P*c2*(P*c3)^{c4}=c2*c3^{c4} P^{c4+1}\). This is fine. So structurally this candidate **can** represent polynomial up to degree 2 plus a fractional power. But GT has a **cubic** term in \(P\) (from expanding the first product gives a \(P^3\) component with nonzero coefficient). Candidate 21 has **no \(P^3\)** term unless \(c4+1=3\) (then it’s \(P^3\) but loses \(P^{1/3}\)). So cannot match both cubic and \(P^{1/3}\) simultaneously. **No**.
